				<div class="page-heading">
					<h1 id="section_0">MGM Resorts International</h1>
					<div class="tagline"></div>
				</div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p><b>MGM Resorts International</b> is an American global <a href="/wiki/Hospitality" title="Hospitality">hospitality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Entertainment" title="Entertainment">entertainment</a> company operating destination resorts in  <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Bellagio_(resort)" title="Bellagio (resort)">Bellagio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay" title="Mandalay Bay">Mandalay Bay</a>,  <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Las_Vegas" title="MGM Grand Las Vegas">MGM Grand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Park_MGM" title="Park MGM">Park MGM</a>. In January 2019 the company took over <a href="/wiki/Empire_City_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire City Casino">Empire City Casino</a> in Yonkers, NY and also recently opened <a href="/wiki/MGM_National_Harbor" title="MGM National Harbor">MGM National Harbor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/MGM_Springfield" title="MGM Springfield">MGM Springfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>. It has a majority interest in MGM China Holdings Limited, which owns the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Macau" title="MGM Macau">MGM Macau</a> resort and casino, and is developing a gaming resort in <a href="/wiki/Cotai" title="Cotai">Cotai</a>. MGM Resorts owns 50 percent of <a href="/wiki/CityCenter" title="CityCenter">CityCenter</a> in Las Vegas, which features <a href="/wiki/Aria_Resort_%26_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Aria Resort &amp; Casino">Aria Resort &amp; Casino</a>. It has a majority controlling interest in <a href="/wiki/MGM_Growth_Properties" title="MGM Growth Properties">MGM Growth Properties</a>, a real estate investment trust.<sup Rowe Price</a> <small>(13.9%)</small><sup id="cite_ref-Proxy2016_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proxy2016-2">[2]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">74,500 (2020)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Division_(business)" title="Division (business)">Divisions</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/MGM_Growth_Properties" title="MGM Growth Properties">MGM Growth Properties</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">MGM Resorts Vacations<br>Diaoyutai MGM Hospitality</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mgmresorts.com">mgmresorts<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>The company began operations in 1987 as <b>MGM Grand, Inc.</b> and became <b>MGM Mirage</b> in 2000, after acquiring <a href="/wiki/Mirage_Resorts" title="Mirage Resorts">Mirage Resorts</a>. In the mid-2000s, growth of its non-gaming (lodging, food, retail) revenue began to outpace gaming receipts and demand for high-rise condominiums was surging, with median property prices in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a> twice the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-houseloses_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houseloses-5">[5]</a></sup>  The company shifted its focus from owning and operating resorts and casinos, to developing and building real estate in the leisure and gaming industry—launching the massive <a href="/wiki/CityCenter" title="CityCenter">CityCenter</a> mixed-use project,<sup id="cite_ref-hbr1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbr1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hbr2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbr2-7">[7]</a></sup> which was at the time of its construction the world's largest construction site and ranks as one of the most expensive real estate projects in history.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> City Center's development coincided with the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">global financial crisis</a>, causing writedowns in its valuation.<sup id="cite_ref-writedownsvaluation_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-writedownsvaluation-9">[9]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2010, the company changed to its present name to reflect its latest strategy of expanding worldwide, including licensing its brand and expertise to develop non-gaming hotels and residences.<sup id="cite_ref-residencesa_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-residencesa-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lvrj1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lvrj1-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lvs1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lvs1-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>Billionaire investor <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Kerkorian" title="Kirk Kerkorian">Kirk Kerkorian</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Tracinda_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Tracinda Corporation">Tracinda Corporation</a> were, until 2009, the majority shareholders of MGM Mirage;  Kerkorian was the former owner of the <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer</a> movie studio, from which MGM Grand derived its name. Following a one-billion-dollar stock offering by MGM Mirage amidst the global credit crunch, Tracinda's shares were diluted from 53.8 percent to 39 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-tracinda_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tracinda-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-moneycnnnews_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moneycnnnews-14">[14]</a></sup> On June 15, 2010, shareholders voted for MGM Mirage to change its name to "MGM Resorts International", which emphasizes the brand's global scope and increased non-gaming strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-fnnegana_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fnnegana-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, MGM won state licenses to build a <a href="/wiki/MGM_National_Harbor" title="MGM National Harbor">$1-billion resort</a> in <a href="/wiki/National_Harbor,_Maryland" title="National Harbor, Maryland">National Harbor, Maryland</a><sup id="cite_ref-dulaca_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dulaca-16">[16]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MGM_Springfield" title="MGM Springfield">a $950-million resort</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-togetstates_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-togetstates-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-selectswhiting_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-selectswhiting-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stutzhoward_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stutzhoward-19">[19]</a></sup> In May 2014, MGM broke ground on a <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_Arena" title="T-Mobile Arena">$375-million arena</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas Strip</a> with sports and entertainment company <a href="/wiki/Anschutz_Entertainment_Group" title="Anschutz Entertainment Group">AEG</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-snellalana_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snellalana-20">[20]</a></sup> MGM Resorts is the majority owner of <a href="/wiki/MGM_Growth_Properties" title="MGM Growth Properties">MGM Growth Properties</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_investment_trust" title="Real estate investment trust">real estate investment trust</a> that owns twelve casino properties and leases them to MGM Resorts. It became a separate, publicly traded company in April 2016.
</p><p>Among the company's management ranks, more than 38 percent are minorities and nearly 43 percent are women.<sup id="cite_ref-mgmrresrots_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgmrresrots-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Background_and_early_ventures_.281969.E2.80.931988.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_early_ventures_(1969–1988)">Background and early ventures (1969–1988)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background and early ventures (1969–1988)" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company's background can be traced to 1969, when airline and casino tycoon <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Kerkorian" title="Kirk Kerkorian">Kirk Kerkorian</a> bought a controlling stake in the <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer</a> (MGM) film studio.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1970 and 1971, Kerkorian struggled with debt from his acquisitions of MGM and <a href="/wiki/Western_Airlines" title="Western Airlines">Western Airlines</a>, and was forced to sell a majority of his casino company, International Leisure, to <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilton Hotels">Hilton Hotels</a> at a steep discount.<sup id="cite_ref-aarons_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aarons-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> When the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Hilton" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas Hilton">Las Vegas Hilton</a>, the casino he had built, subsequently became the most successful hotel in Las Vegas, Kerkorian was inspired to lead the studio into the gambling industry.<sup id="cite_ref-aarons_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aarons-23">[23]</a></sup> It opened the original <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Hotel_and_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM Grand Hotel and Casino">MGM Grand Hotel and Casino</a> (now Bally's Las Vegas) in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Reno" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM Grand Reno">MGM Grand Reno</a> followed in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p><br>
By 1979, the two hotel-casinos accounted for most of MGM's income, and the company announced a plan to split itself in two.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The next year, the film studio was <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spun off</a> as a new company, while the original company, renamed as MGM Grand Hotels Inc., retained the two hotel-casinos.<sup id="cite_ref-hollie_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollie-28">[28]</a></sup> Kerkorian held a 47 percent stake in both companies.<sup id="cite_ref-hollie_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollie-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>In 1985, Kerkorian began seeking a buyer for MGM Grand Hotels, to allow him to concentrate on running <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a> and on developing new properties under the MGM Grand name.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> A deal was reached for <a href="/wiki/Bally_Manufacturing" title="Bally Manufacturing">Bally Manufacturing</a> to buy the company; the deal closed in April 1986,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and the two casinos were renamed under the Bally's brand.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The terms of the sale allowed Kerkorian to retain rights to the MGM Grand name, and plans were announced to offer the stockholders of MGM Grand Hotels shares in a new company that would hold the naming rights.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>The company now known as MGM Resorts International was formed in 1986 as <b>Grand Name Co.</b><sup id="cite_ref-edgar94_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edgar94-33">[33]</a></sup> as a subsidiary of Kerkorian's <a href="/wiki/Tracinda_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Tracinda Corporation">Tracinda Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> It was renamed the following year as <b>MGM Grand, Inc.</b><sup id="cite_ref-edgar94_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edgar94-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>The company's first venture was <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Air" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM Grand Air">MGM Grand Air</a>, a luxury airline offering service between New York and Los Angeles, which launched in September 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The company also made an offer to take over financially struggling <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a>, but it was rejected by Pan Am's board in November 1987 for being too conditional.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p><p>In August 1987, MGM Grand bid $152 million for the bankrupt <a href="/wiki/Dunes_(hotel_and_casino)" title="Dunes (hotel and casino)">Dunes Hotel</a> in Las Vegas, but was beat out by Japanese billionaire Masao Nangaku.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Instead, the company acquired the <a href="/wiki/Desert_Inn" title="Desert Inn">Desert Inn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sands_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Sands Hotel">Sands</a> casinos in February 1988 from <a href="/wiki/Summa_Corporation" title="Summa Corporation">Summa Corporation</a> for $167 million.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The Sands was promptly sold to <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Adelson" title="Sheldon Adelson">Sheldon Adelson</a>'s Interface Group for $110 million in April 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="First_casino_developments_.281989.E2.80.931999.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_casino_developments_(1989–1999)">First casino developments (1989–1999)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First casino developments (1989–1999)" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In September 1989, the company announced plans for a $700-million Hollywood-themed complex, including a 4,000-room hotel and a theme park.<sup id="cite_ref-turner_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turner-40">[40]</a></sup> The Desert Inn site was initially considered as a location for the project,<sup id="cite_ref-turner_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turner-40">[40]</a></sup> but within weeks the location was finalized as the <a href="/wiki/Marina_Hotel_and_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Marina Hotel and Casino">Marina Hotel and Casino</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Country_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropicana Country Club">Tropicana Country Club</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> which MGM Grand acquired for $93 million plus $30 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The company put the Desert Inn up for sale to focus efforts on the new project,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> but found no outside bidders, and agreed to sell it to Tracinda for $130 million.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Construction on the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Las_Vegas" title="MGM Grand Las Vegas">MGM Grand Las Vegas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Adventures_Theme_Park" title="MGM Grand Adventures Theme Park">MGM Grand Adventures</a> theme park began in October 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and the property opened in December 1993 at a final cost of $1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The park permanently closed in 2002 due to a lack of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-sun2012_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sun2012-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>The company moved its headquarters from Beverly Hills to Las Vegas in July 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>During construction of the MGM Grand, the company acquired an option to buy an 18-acre site across the street from the project.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Primm" title="Gary Primm">Gary Primm</a> of <a href="/wiki/Primadonna_Resorts" class="mw-redirect" title="Primadonna Resorts">Primadonna Resorts</a> approached MGM president Bob Maxey in 1994 with an idea for the site: a casino recreating the New York skyline.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> A joint venture was formed between the two companies, and construction began in March 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Completed at a cost of $460 million, the <a href="/wiki/New_York-New_York_Hotel_and_Casino" title="New York-New York Hotel and Casino">New York-New York Hotel and Casino</a> opened in January 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>With New York-New York under development, MGM Grand made moves to expand in several other markets. An exploratory agreement to develop two casinos on the Chinese island of <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a> was announced in August 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> but came to nothing. In <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Darwin, Australia">Darwin, Australia</a>, a lucrative market attracting high rollers from Pacific Rim countries,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> the company considered building a hotel,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> but instead bought the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Darwin" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM Grand Darwin">Diamond Beach Hotel and Casino</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> renaming it as the MGM Grand Darwin. MGM announced plans for an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic City">Atlantic City</a> casino in July 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In Michigan, where voters approved casinos in November 1996, MGM made plans for a bid on one of the three available gaming licenses,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> which would eventually be approved and open in July 1999 as the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Detroit" title="MGM Grand Detroit">MGM Grand Detroit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, with casino gambling newly authorized, MGM announced plans in August 1996 to develop 15 properties in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Tsogo_Sun" title="Tsogo Sun">Tsogo Sun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The first, a temporary casino in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Dome" class="mw-redirect" title="Coca-Cola Dome">Sundome</a>, opened in October 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Three more casinos followed before MGM agreed to sell out its interest in the properties to Tsogo Sun in November 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>Since the initiation of New York-New York, analysts had speculated that MGM Grand or Primadonna would buy out the other's interest in the project.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Instead of making such a cash-intensive purchase,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> however, MGM agreed to buy Primadonna outright for $276 million in stock plus $336 million in assumed debt.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The merger closed in March 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> giving MGM ownership of three casinos and two golf courses at the Nevada–California state line, in addition to full control of New York-New York.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Mirage_Resorts_merger_.282000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mirage_Resorts_merger_(2000)">Mirage Resorts merger (2000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mirage Resorts merger (2000)" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In February 2000, MGM Grand made an unsolicited offer of $17 a share to buy <a href="/wiki/Mirage_Resorts" title="Mirage Resorts">Mirage Resorts</a>, which had foundered due to disappointing results at its new <a href="/wiki/Beau_Rivage_(Mississippi)" title="Beau Rivage (Mississippi)">Beau Rivage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bellagio_(resort_and_casino)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellagio (resort and casino)">Bellagio</a> resorts.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Analysts expected a protracted battle, with Mirage founder <a href="/wiki/Steve_Wynn" title="Steve Wynn">Steve Wynn</a> seen as unwilling to give up control but under pressure from institutional investors.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Mirage rejected the offer,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> but Wynn met with Kerkorian the next day and named a price of $21 a share.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The companies agreed on the higher price, for a total of $4.4 billion plus $2 billion in assumed debt.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The merger closed in May 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> giving MGM ownership of the <a href="/wiki/The_Mirage" title="The Mirage">Mirage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Treasure_Island_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Treasure Island Hotel and Casino">Treasure Island</a>, Bellagio, <a href="/wiki/Boardwalk_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Boardwalk Hotel and Casino">Boardwalk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Nugget_Las_Vegas" title="Golden Nugget Las Vegas">Golden Nugget</a> casinos in Las Vegas, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Nugget_Laughlin" title="Golden Nugget Laughlin">Golden Nugget</a> in Laughlin, and the Beau Rivage in Mississippi, and a half share of the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Resort_and_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Monte Carlo Resort and Casino">Monte Carlo</a>. The company changed its name to MGM Mirage in August 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Mirage had also owned a half stake in the <a href="/wiki/Borgata" title="Borgata">Borgata</a>, a planned casino in Atlantic City, in a joint venture managed by <a href="/wiki/Boyd_Gaming" title="Boyd Gaming">Boyd Gaming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Work on the Borgata continued apace, and it would open in July 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Stalled_developments_.282001.E2.80.932004.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stalled_developments_(2001–2004)">Stalled developments (2001–2004)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Stalled developments (2001–2004)" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2001 and 2002, following the merger with Mirage, the company explored options for its next major development project, including opportunities in the Las Vegas, Atlantic City, Chicago, and Macau markets.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The 55-acre site of the Boardwalk casino on the Las Vegas Strip was earmarked for a technologically advanced megaresort targeting a <a href="/wiki/Generation_X" title="Generation X">Generation X</a> demographic.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In Atlantic City, MGM shifted focus from its previously announced boardwalk site to a proposed billion-dollar hotel and casino on a 55-acre tract adjacent to the Borgata, where Wynn had planned to build the Le Jardin casino.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In the Chicago market, MGM agreed to pay $600 million to buy the unfinished Emerald Casino in <a href="/wiki/Rosemont,_Illinois" title="Rosemont, Illinois">Rosemont, Illinois</a>, whose investors had been accused of ties to organized crime.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The deal was rejected, however, by state gaming regulators,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and MGM then backed off its effort, saying that Illinois's casino tax was too high.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In Macau, where <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Ho" title="Stanley Ho">Stanley Ho</a>'s 40-year government-granted monopoly on gambling was coming to an end, MGM submitted a bid for one of three available gaming concessions,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> but it was not selected, losing out to Ho, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Sands" title="Las Vegas Sands">Las Vegas Sands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wynn_Resorts" title="Wynn Resorts">Wynn Resorts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p><p>MGM made moves into the United Kingdom market after a 2001 government report called for loosening of the country's gambling regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-benston_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-benston-86">[86]</a></sup> It opened an online casino, playmgmmirage.com, licensed in the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, a British dependency,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and it applied for a license to run an online sports betting site in the U.K.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> It acquired a twenty-five percent stake in a company developing the small Triangle Casino in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-benston_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-benston-86">[86]</a></sup> which went on to open its doors in February 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> It inked deals to build casinos at the <a href="/wiki/Olympia_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympia (London)">Olympia Exhibition Centre</a> in London,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James' Park">St James' Park</a> in Newcastle,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Meadowhall Shopping Centre">Meadowhall Shopping Centre</a> in Sheffield,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/National_Exhibition_Centre" title="National Exhibition Centre">National Exhibition Centre</a> in Birmingham,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sportcity" title="Sportcity">Sportcity</a> in Manchester, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Harbour" title="Glasgow Harbour">Glasgow Harbour</a>, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Dock,_Port_of_Liverpool" title="King's Dock, Port of Liverpool">King's Waterfront</a> in Liverpool, and at a proposed stadium in <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Salford, Greater Manchester">Salford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The company also signed a $490-million deal to acquire Wembley plc, owner of seven <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_racing" title="Greyhound racing">greyhound tracks</a> in Britain and four in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p><p>The British expansion plans ultimately amounted to nothing. MGM closed its online casino after less than two years, citing uncertainty in American regulations and competition from established British brands.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The Wembley acquisition turned into a bidding war, with MGM finally losing out to an investors group including Kerzner International.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The Triangle Casino was sold off to <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Leisure" title="Stanley Leisure">Stanley Leisure</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The company's other development plans were scuttled as the government scaled down, and eventually abandoned, the plan to allow large "<a href="/wiki/Supercasino" class="mw-redirect" title="Supercasino">super-casinos</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>On December 20, 2003, MGM and <a href="/wiki/Turnberry_Associates" title="Turnberry Associates">Turnberry Associates</a> announced the formation of a partnership to build the luxury condo hotel, stating that they would build up to six towers each rising up to 40 stories. On May 12, 2006, the first tower opened for occupancy. The successful opening of <a href="/wiki/The_Signature_at_MGM_Grand" title="The Signature at MGM Grand">The Signature at MGM Grand</a> appears to be aided by its connection to the resources and amenities of <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Las_Vegas" title="MGM Grand Las Vegas">The MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino</a>.
</p><p>In 2004, the company disposed of some of its smaller properties, selling the two Golden Nugget casinos (<a href="/wiki/Golden_Nugget_Las_Vegas" title="Golden Nugget Las Vegas">Golden Nugget Las Vegas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Nugget_Laughlin" title="Golden Nugget Laughlin">Golden Nugget Laughlin</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Poster_Financial_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Poster Financial Group">Poster Financial Group</a> for $215 million,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Darwin" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM Grand Darwin">MGM Grand Darwin</a> to <a href="/wiki/Skycity_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Skycity Entertainment">Skycity Entertainment</a> for $140 million.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Mandalay_merger_.282004.E2.80.932005.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mandalay_merger_(2004–2005)">Mandalay merger (2004–2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mandalay merger (2004–2005)" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MGM entered into quiet merger talks with <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Resort_Group" title="Mandalay Resort Group">Mandalay Resort Group</a> in early 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-mylchreest_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mylchreest-103">[103]</a></sup> The potential acquisition, which would give MGM control of more than half the hotel rooms on the Las Vegas Strip,<sup id="cite_ref-binkley_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-binkley-104">[104]</a></sup> was seen as a "vote" for Las Vegas as the strongest gambling market in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Mandalay assets attractive to MGM included low-end casinos like <a href="/wiki/Excalibur_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Excalibur Hotel and Casino">Excalibur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Circus_Circus_Las_Vegas" title="Circus Circus Las Vegas">Circus Circus</a> to broaden MGM's "high roller" appeal;<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay_Convention_Center" title="Mandalay Bay Convention Center">Mandalay Bay Convention Center</a>, which would allow MGM to compete directly with the <a href="/wiki/Sands_Expo" title="Sands Expo">Sands Expo</a> center in the convention market;<sup id="cite_ref-binkley_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-binkley-104">[104]</a></sup> and at least two prime developable sites on the Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The talks went public in June, when MGM announced an offer worth $7.65 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-fizzle_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fizzle-108">[108]</a></sup> Mandalay rejected that offer because of a clause allowing MGM to back out if <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> regulators demanded the sale of any properties.<sup id="cite_ref-fizzle_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fizzle-108">[108]</a></sup> Analysts speculated that another bidder such as <a href="/wiki/Harrah%27s_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Harrah's Entertainment">Harrah's</a> or Boyd might enter, but none did,<sup id="cite_ref-mylchreest_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mylchreest-103">[103]</a></sup> and MGM and Mandalay soon agreed on a $7.9 billion deal.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>MGM executives were confident that antitrust regulators would not require the sale of any of the two companies' properties.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Michigan law, however, forbade one company from owning multiple casinos, requiring the sale of either the MGM Grand Detroit or Mandalay's 54 percent stake in the <a href="/wiki/MotorCity_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="MotorCity Casino">MotorCity Casino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> After some vacillation about which property to sell,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Mandalay accepted a $525-million offer for its interest in MotorCity from <a href="/wiki/Marian_Ilitch" title="Marian Ilitch">Marian Ilitch</a>, the casino's second largest shareholder.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in Illinois, where MGM needed regulatory approval to take over Mandalay's 50 percent interest in the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Victoria_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Victoria Casino">Grand Victoria Casino</a>, a lack of <a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a> on the state Gaming Board threatened to delay the merger.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> MGM considered a sale to the casino's other owner, the <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_family" title="Pritzker family">Pritzker family</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> but ultimately gained approval for a plan to place the property under control of a <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustee</a> until completion of the licensing process.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The FTC approved the merger as predicted,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and MGM obtained a $7 billion <a href="/wiki/Line_of_credit" title="Line of credit">line of credit</a> to finance it.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The sale closed on April 25, 2005 for a total of $7.9 billion, including $3 billion in assumed debt.<sup id="cite_ref-smith_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-119">[119]</a></sup></p><p>The Mandalay acquisition made MGM Mirage the largest gaming company in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-smith_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-119">[119]</a></sup> but it was surpassed just two months later when Harrah's Entertainment acquired <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Entertainment,_Inc." title="Caesars Entertainment, Inc.">Caesars Entertainment</a><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> in a deal that had been spurred on by news of the MGM-Mandalay merger.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Later_developments_.282004.E2.80.932006.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_developments_(2004–2006)">Later developments (2004–2006)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Later developments (2004–2006)" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MGM_Mirage_Corporate_Support_Center.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/MGM_Mirage_Corporate_Support_Center.jpg/220px-MGM_Mirage_Corporate_Support_Center.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/MGM_Mirage_Corporate_Support_Center.jpg/220px-MGM_Mirage_Corporate_Support_Center.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MGM_Mirage_Corporate_Support_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MGM Mirage's Corporate Support Center in <a href="/wiki/Paradise,_Nevada" title="Paradise, Nevada">Paradise, Nevada</a></div></div></div>
<p>Despite MGM's initial failure to win a gaming concession in Macau, the company had remained interested in the burgeoning gaming market. Rumors of a possible partnership with Stanley Ho were reported in 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> but Nevada gaming regulators informally vetoed the idea because of the alleged involvement of organized crime <a href="/wiki/Triad_(organized_crime)" title="Triad (organized crime)">triads</a> in his casinos.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Another possibility emerged when the government allowed the three gaming concessionaires to each sell a sub-concession.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In June 2004, MGM formed a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Pansy_Ho" title="Pansy Ho">Pansy Ho</a>, Stanley's daughter, to develop a casino-hotel under a sub-concession from Stanley.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Despite initial concerns about whether Pansy Ho was subject to her father's influence, the Nevada Gaming Commission eventually approved the partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Construction of the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Macau" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM Grand Macau">MGM Grand Macau</a> began in June 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The property opened in December 2007, completed at a cost of $1.25 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p><p>In 2004, MGM solidified its plans for the Boardwalk site on the Strip, announcing <a href="/wiki/Project_CityCenter" class="mw-redirect" title="Project CityCenter">Project CityCenter</a>, an $8-billion high-density project including hotels, condominiums, a casino, and a shopping mall.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup>  The Boardwalk was closed in January 2006 to make way for the redevelopment,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and CityCenter construction began the following June.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> emerged in 2004 as the next major new Asian gaming market, calling for proposals to build two "<a href="/wiki/Integrated_resort" title="Integrated resort">integrated resort</a>" casinos at <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay,_Singapore" title="Marina Bay, Singapore">Marina Bay</a> and the island of <a href="/wiki/Sentosa" title="Sentosa">Sentosa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mihailovich_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mihailovich-133">[133]</a></sup> MGM partnered with <a href="/wiki/CapitaLand" title="CapitaLand">CapitaLand</a> in an estimated $3 billion<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> bid for the Marina Bay site.<sup id="cite_ref-mihailovich_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mihailovich-133">[133]</a></sup> Their bid advanced to the final stage against three competitors, and was seen as the favorite to win.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The government awarded the license, however, to <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Sands" title="Las Vegas Sands">Las Vegas Sands</a>, citing its strength in the <a href="/wiki/Meetings,_incentives,_conferencing,_exhibitions" title="Meetings, incentives, conferencing, exhibitions">meetings and conventions</a> sector.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p><p>On April 25, 2006, MGM Mirage announced with <a href="/wiki/Foxwoods_Resort_Casino" title="Foxwoods Resort Casino">Foxwoods Resort and Casino</a> a joint partnership in developing an expansion plan at Foxwoods that will include a casino using the MGM Grand brand.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> On October 16, 2006, MGM Mirage announced that it planned to sell its properties in <a href="/wiki/Laughlin,_Nevada" title="Laughlin, Nevada">Laughlin</a>  (<a href="/wiki/Colorado_Belle_Hotel_%26_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado Belle Hotel &amp; Casino">Colorado Belle Hotel &amp; Casino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edgewater_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Edgewater Hotel and Casino">Edgewater Hotel and Casino</a>) to a partnership of Anthony Marnell III and Sher Gaming.  The sale price was $200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The sale closed on June 1, 2007.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On October 31, 2006, MGM Mirage announced plans to sell <a href="/wiki/Primadonna_Resorts" class="mw-redirect" title="Primadonna Resorts">Primm Valley Resorts</a> to <a href="/wiki/Herbst_Gaming" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbst Gaming">Herbst Gaming</a> for $400 million.  The proposed sale would not include the <a href="/wiki/Primm_Valley_Golf_Club" title="Primm Valley Golf Club">Primm Valley Golf Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup>  The sale closed on April 10, 2007.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Landing_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Nevada Landing Hotel and Casino">Nevada Landing Hotel and Casino</a> closed a month earlier than planned on March 20, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Dubai_World_investment_.282007.E2.80.932009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dubai_World_investment_(2007–2009)">Dubai World investment (2007–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dubai World investment (2007–2009)" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On April 19, 2007 the company announced that it planned to purchase a 7.6-acre (31,000 m<sup>2</sup>) site from Concord Wilshire Partners for $130 million and a 25.8-acre (104,000 m<sup>2</sup>) site from Gordon Gaming for $444 million.  The two parcels give the company complete control of the southwest corner of the Sahara and Las Vegas Boulevard intersection.  When combined with underused parts of the <a href="/wiki/Circus_Circus_Las_Vegas" title="Circus Circus Las Vegas">Circus Circus</a> site, the company will have a 68-acre (280,000 m<sup>2</sup>) site for future development.  The Concord site had been the proposed location for the <b>Maxim Casino</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p><p>On August 22, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Dubai_World" title="Dubai World">Dubai World</a> said it would buy a 9.5 percent stake in MGM for about $2.4 billion. It would also invest about $2.7 billion to acquire a 50 percent stake in MGM's CityCenter project. Dubai World would pay MGM Mirage an additional $100 million if the project opened on time and on budget. The investment firm would buy 14.2 million shares from MGM Mirage. The firm would also issue a public tender for an additional 14.2 million shares at the same price.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg/220px-MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="31" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="248" data-file-height="35"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 31px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg/220px-MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="31" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg/330px-MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg/440px-MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MGM_Mirage_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old MGM Mirage logo</div></div></div>
<p>On October 29, 2008, MGM Mirage halted a $5 billion Atlantic City <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Atlantic_City" title="MGM Grand Atlantic City">project</a> on land next to the Borgata.
</p><p>At about the same time, New Jersey gambling regulators were evaluating MGM Mirage's suitability to operate casinos in New Jersey, and were unconvinced that MGM Mirage's Macau partner, Pansy Ho, could operate independently from influence of her father, Stanley Ho.  The latter was often accused of ties with Chinese organized crime and letting the gangs operate in his casinos' VIP rooms. Faced with not complying with New Jersey gaming regulations, MGM Mirage decided to divest the highly profitable Borgata in order to continue pursuing the even more lucrative Chinese market.<sup id="cite_ref-AOL1_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOL1-143">[143]</a></sup>  MGM Mirage subsequently transferred its 50% share in the Borgata to a divestiture trust through which it received all benefit of the ownership.  The trust was responsible for selling MGM's interest within 30 months, although MGM had the right to direct the trustee during the first 18 months.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p><p>On December 16, 2008, MGM Mirage announced the sale of its Las Vegas <a href="/wiki/Treasure_Island_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Treasure Island Hotel and Casino">Treasure Island</a> resort and casino to billionaire <a href="/wiki/Phil_Ruffin" title="Phil Ruffin">Phil Ruffin</a>. The sale was completed on March 20, 2009 for $600 million in cash plus a $175 million promissory note.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p><p>On March 23, 2009 Dubai World and Infinity World announced that they had filed a lawsuit in the Delaware Chancery Court seeking to be released from their CityCenter joint venture agreement with MGM Mirage after the company filed its annual report stating that "there is substantial doubt about our ability to continue as a going concern," and "it cannot provide assurance that its business would generate sufficient cash flow from operation."<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p><p>Starting on April 6, 2009 news reports surfaced that MGM Mirage had hired investment firm <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a> to assist the company in finding possible buyers for the MGM Grand Detroit and the Beau Rivage.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Name_change_and_recent_years_.282010.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_change_and_recent_years_(2010–present)">Name change and recent years (2010–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Name change and recent years (2010–present)" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On June 15, 2010, shareholders approved a name change from MGM Mirage to "MGM Resorts International", to emphasize the brand's global scope and increased non-gaming strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-lvrj1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lvrj1-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2011 an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> was announced for the MGM Macau property. Under the agreement, Pansy Ho would receive a 29 percent stake in the company, MGM China Holdings Ltd, which was created as a listing vehicle for the IPO. MGM Resorts would hold 51 percent and the public would receive 20 percent. MGM China raised $1.5 billion from its IPO on the Hong Kong Stock Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> In January 2013, MGM China received government approval to build its second resort in Macau.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2013, Maryland awarded the company a license to build <a href="/wiki/MGM_National_Harbor" title="MGM National Harbor">MGM National Harbor</a>, a $1-billion casino resort at <a href="/wiki/National_Harbor,_Maryland" title="National Harbor, Maryland">National Harbor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George's County, Maryland">Prince George's County, Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Also in late 2013, Foxwoods and MGM ended their relationship, and the MGM Grand at Foxwoods was renamed the Fox Tower.<sup id="cite_ref-courant_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courant-158">[158]</a></sup></p><p>On May 1, 2014, the company broke ground on the $375-million <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_Arena" title="T-Mobile Arena">T-Mobile Arena</a> located behind New-New York Hotel and Casino, in partnership with <a href="/wiki/AEG_Live" class="mw-redirect" title="AEG Live">AEG Live</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> The arena opened on April 6, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-T_Moblie_Arena_Opening_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T_Moblie_Arena_Opening-160">[160]</a></sup> In September 2014, MGM purchased the <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> for a new baseball stadium in Biloxi, resulting in <a href="/wiki/MGM_Park" title="MGM Park">MGM Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> That same year, the Massachusetts Gaming Commission approved a license for <a href="/wiki/MGM_Springfield" title="MGM Springfield">MGM Springfield</a>, an $800-million project.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p><p>MGM sold several properties in 2015, including the <a href="/wiki/Railroad_Pass_Casino" title="Railroad Pass Casino">Railroad Pass Casino</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Strike_Hotel_and_Gambling_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Strike Hotel and Gambling Hall">Gold Strike</a>, <sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> and properties in <a href="/wiki/Reno" class="mw-redirect" title="Reno">Reno</a> (<a href="/wiki/Circus_Circus_Reno" title="Circus Circus Reno">Circus Circus Reno</a> and a 50 percent stake in the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Legacy_Reno" class="mw-redirect" title="Silver Legacy Reno">Silver Legacy</a>) were sold to <a href="/wiki/Eldorado_Resorts" title="Eldorado Resorts">Eldorado Resorts</a> for $72.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2016, MGM held an initial public offering for <a href="/wiki/MGM_Growth_Properties" title="MGM Growth Properties">MGM Growth Properties</a> (MGP), a new <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_investment_trust" title="Real estate investment trust">real estate investment trust</a> (REIT) with ownership of ten of the company's casinos; the parent company would continue to operate the casinos under a lease agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hirsch_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hirsch-172">[172]</a></sup> The offering raised $1.05 billion, and left MGM Resorts with 76 percent ownership of the REIT.<sup id="cite_ref-hirsch_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hirsch-172">[172]</a></sup> In June 2016, MGM announced a joint venture with Sydell Group to renovate and rebrand the Monte Carlo as the Park MGM, named after the adjacent dining and entertainment district, The Park, that opened in April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> In August 2016, MGM bought out Boyd Gaming's interest in the Borgata for $900 million, and then sold the property to MGP for $1.2 billion and leased it back for $100 million per year.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p><p>In 2017, MGM launched two online ventures under the PlayMGM brand: an online sportsbook in Nevada, and an online casino in New Jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> In October 2017, MGM purchased the <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_Stars" title="San Antonio Stars">San Antonio Stars</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">Women's National Basketball Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> The team was moved to <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay_Events_Center" title="Mandalay Bay Events Center">Mandalay Bay Events Center</a> and began play as the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Aces" title="Las Vegas Aces">Las Vegas Aces</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2018, MGM announced a 50/50 joint venture with UK gambling operator <a href="/wiki/GVC_Holdings" title="GVC Holdings">GVC Holdings</a> to create a sports betting and online gaming platform targeting the U.S. market in states where such activities are legal.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> In January 2019, the joint venture was named Roar Digital.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> In August 2018, MGM and Hyatt sold the Grand Victoria Casino to Eldorado Resorts for $328 million.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p><p>Following the U.S. Supreme Court’s May 2018 ruling that struck down the <a href="/wiki/Professional_and_Amateur_Sports_Protection_Act_of_1992" title="Professional and Amateur Sports Protection Act of 1992">PASPA</a> sports betting ban, MGM announced official partnerships with several North American professional sports leagues, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> In March 2019, MGM announced an official gaming partnership with <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2019, MGM bought <a href="/wiki/Yonkers_Raceway" class="mw-redirect" title="Yonkers Raceway">Yonkers Raceway and Empire City Casino</a> in New York from the <a href="/wiki/Rooney_family" title="Rooney family">Rooney family</a> for $850 million, and then immediately sold the land and buildings to MGP for $625 million, and leased them back for $50 million per year.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mgm2019_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgm2019-190">[190]</a></sup></p><p>At the end of October 2019, MGM established a betting partnership with Yahoo Sports to connect its sports betting online platform to the popular sports website<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="MGM_Hospitality">MGM Hospitality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: MGM Hospitality" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>In 2007, MGM Hospitality was established to operate hotels, resorts and residences in key destinations around the globe using the brands of <a href="/wiki/Bellagio_(resort)" title="Bellagio (resort)">Bellagio</a>, <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Las_Vegas" title="MGM Grand Las Vegas">MGM Grand</a> and Skylofts.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, the company formed Diaoyutai MGM Hospitality, a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Diaoyutai_State_Guesthouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Diaoyutai State Guesthouse">Diaoyutai State Guesthouse</a> of China (the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Foreign_Ministry" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Foreign Ministry">Chinese Foreign Ministry</a>’s venue for VIPs).  This joint venture is developing and operating 5-star hotels and resorts in China.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, MGM and Hakkasan Group announced the formation of a joint venture named MGM Hakkasan Hospitality, which would develop non-gaming hotels around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The partnership was terminated a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="MGM_Resorts_International_properties">MGM Resorts International properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: MGM Resorts International properties" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>All properties are wholly owned by MGM Resorts International except where indicated.
</p>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Borgata" title="Borgata">Borgata</a> – <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">Atlantic City, New Jersey</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Yonkers_Raceway" class="mw-redirect" title="Yonkers Raceway">Yonkers Raceway &amp; Empire City Casino</a> – <a href="/wiki/Yonkers,_New_York" title="Yonkers, New York">Yonkers, New York</a></li>
<li>72 acres (29 ha) of land for the undeveloped <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Atlantic_City" title="MGM Grand Atlantic City">MGM Grand Atlantic City</a></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Golf_courses">Golf courses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Golf courses" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li>Dragon Ridge Country Club – <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas, Nevada</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Festival_Grounds" title="Las Vegas Festival Grounds">Las Vegas Festival Grounds</a></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="MGM_Mirage_Aviation">MGM Mirage Aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: MGM Mirage Aviation" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The MGM Resorts International Aviation fleet comprises five aircraft (as of August 2017): a <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_G550" title="Gulfstream G550">Gulfstream G550</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Embraer_Legacy_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Embraer Legacy 500">Embraer Legacy 500</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Embraer_Lineage_1000" title="Embraer Lineage 1000">Embraer Lineage 1000</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff_and_management">Staff and management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Staff and management" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>The company’s top executives include: <a href="/wiki/James_Murren" title="James Murren">James Murren</a>, chairman and chief executive officer; <a href="/wiki/William_Hornbuckle" title="William Hornbuckle">Bill Hornbuckle</a>, president of global casino marketing; <a href="/wiki/Brian_Sandoval" title="Brian Sandoval">Brian Sandoval</a>, president of global gambling development; <a href="/wiki/Corey_I._Sanders" title="Corey I. Sanders">Corey I. Sanders</a>, chief operating officer; and John McManus, executive vice president, general counsel and secretary.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p><p>Among the company's management ranks, more than 38 percent are minorities and nearly 43 percent are women.<sup id="cite_ref-mgmrresrots_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgmrresrots-21">[21]</a></sup> The company has received wide recognition for its diversity and inclusion initiatives, such as: 40 Best Companies for Diversity (Black Enterprise Magazine),<sup id="cite_ref-blacenterpirse_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blacenterpirse-204">[204]</a></sup> Top 10 Companies for Latinos (DiversityInc Magazine),<sup id="cite_ref-latinsdiveristyinc_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latinsdiveristyinc-205">[205]</a></sup> Best Places to Work for LGBT Equality (Human Rights Campaign Foundation),<sup id="cite_ref-hrcresources_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrcresources-206">[206]</a></sup> Top 10 Regional Companies(DiversityInc)<sup id="cite_ref-diversityimain_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversityimain-207">[207]</a></sup> Top 100 Companies for MBA Students (Universum Global) and Top Corporation for Women's Business Enterprises (Women's Business Enterprise National Council).<sup id="cite_ref-WBENC_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WBENC-208">[208]</a></sup> <i>Fortune</i> magazine named MGM Resorts one of the World’s Most Admired Companies in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-fortunemagazine_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortunemagazine-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controversy" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>MGM Resorts International received criticism for filing a lawsuit on July 18, 2018 against survivors and relatives of victims slain in the October 1, <a href="/wiki/2017_Las_Vegas_shooting" title="2017 Las Vegas shooting">2017 Las Vegas shooting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> MGM has claimed that, because it utilized the security services of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Services_Corporation" title="Contemporary Services Corporation">Contemporary Services Corporation</a>, a vendor certified by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> at the time of the October 1 shooting, any proceedings should be held in federal court where MGM is shielded from liability by the <a href="/wiki/Support_Anti-Terrorism_by_Fostering_Effective_Technologies_Act" title="Support Anti-Terrorism by Fostering Effective Technologies Act">Support Anti-Terrorism by Fostering Effective Technologies Act</a>, also known as the Safety Act.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> MGM said they are insured for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a> 751 million towards the settlement of the lawsuit which MGM believes will be settled in May 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Robert Englet, an attorney to some of the survivors, describes the countersuit as an attempt to get a more favorable judge.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Brian Claypool, another attorney of the survivors', called the lawsuits a “public relations nightmare”.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> MGM's controversial action has prompted a public outcry from survivors of the shooting, family members of the victims, lawmakers, and media members in New York State urging the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Gaming_Commission" title="New York State Gaming Commission">New York State Gaming Commission</a> to block MGM from completing its $850 million deal to purchase <a href="/wiki/Empire_City_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire City Casino">Empire City Casino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yonkers_Raceway" class="mw-redirect" title="Yonkers Raceway">Yonkers Raceway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yonkers,_New_York" title="Yonkers, New York">Yonkers, New York</a>, which deal had been scheduled to close in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_recognition">Awards and recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Awards and recognition" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>The company continues to receive wide recognition for its diversity and inclusion initiatives, such as: 40 Best Companies for Diversity (<i>Black Enterprise Magazine</i>) in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-blacenterpirse_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blacenterpirse-204">[204]</a></sup> Best Places to Work for LGBT Equality (<a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Rights Campaign Foundation">Human Rights Campaign Foundation</a>) in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-hrcresources_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrcresources-206">[206]</a></sup> Top 10 Regional Companies (<i>DiversityInc</i>) in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-diversityimain_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversityimain-207">[207]</a></sup> Top 10 Companies for Latinos (<i>DiversityInc Magazine</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-latinsdiveristyinc_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latinsdiveristyinc-205">[205]</a></sup>  and top 100 Companies for MBA Students (Universum Global) in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-cnnmoney_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnmoney-217">[217]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> has named MGM Resorts one of the World’s Most Admired Companies.<sup id="cite_ref-fortunemagazine_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortunemagazine-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MGM_Resorts_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: References" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
